# Error Handling in Python - Practice Materials

## Practice Exercises

### Exercise 1: Identifying Error Types
**Type**: Multiple Choice
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 5 minutes

**Instructions**: Identify the type of error in each of the following code snippets.

1.  `print(variable_name)`  (where `variable_name` has not been defined)
    A) `TypeError`
    B) `NameError`
    C) `ValueError`
    D) `IndexError`

2.  `result = 10 / 0`
    A) `TypeError`
    B) `ValueError`
    C) `ZeroDivisionError`
    D) `IndexError`

3.  `my_list = [1, 2, 3]`
    `print(my_list[3])`
    A) `TypeError`
    B) `ValueError`
    C) `KeyError`
    D) `IndexError`

**Solution Rubric**:
*   1 point for each correct answer.

### Exercise 2: Basic Try-Except Block
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 10 minutes

**Instructions**: Write a Python program that takes two numbers as input from the user and divides the first number by the second. Use a `try-except` block to handle the potential `ZeroDivisionError`. If a `ZeroDivisionError` occurs, print an appropriate error message.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                 | Points | Description                                                                                                   |
| ------------------------ | ------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Correct Input            | 2      | Program correctly takes two numerical inputs from the user.                                                   |
| Try-Except Implementation | 4      | Program uses a `try-except` block to handle potential `ZeroDivisionError`.                                    |
| Error Handling           | 2      | Program correctly catches the `ZeroDivisionError` and prints an appropriate message.                           |
| Correct Division         | 2      | Program correctly calculates and prints the result of the division if no error occurs.                         |

**Expected Answer Outline**:

```python
try:
    num1 = float(input("Enter the first number: "))
    num2 = float(input("Enter the second number: "))
    result = num1 / num2
    print("Result:", result)
except ZeroDivisionError:
    print("Error: Cannot divide by zero.")
except ValueError:
    print("Error: Invalid input. Please enter numbers only.")
```

### Exercise 3: Handling Multiple Exceptions
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 15 minutes

**Instructions**: Write a Python program that reads a number from a file named "numbers.txt" and converts it to an integer. Handle the following exceptions:

*   `FileNotFoundError`: If the file does not exist.
*   `ValueError`: If the content of the file is not a valid integer.

Print appropriate error messages for each case.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                 | Points | Description                                                                                                   |
| ------------------------ | ------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| File Handling            | 3      | Program correctly opens and attempts to read from the file.                                                   |
| Try-Except Implementation | 3      | Program uses a `try-except` block to handle `FileNotFoundError` and `ValueError`.                             |
| Error Handling           | 4      | Program correctly catches both exceptions and prints appropriate messages.                                       |

**Expected Answer Outline**:

```python
try:
    with open("numbers.txt", "r") as file:
        number_str = file.readline().strip()
        number = int(number_str)
        print("Number:", number)
except FileNotFoundError:
    print("Error: File not found.")
except ValueError:
    print("Error: Invalid content in the file. Please provide a valid integer.")
```

### Exercise 4: `else` and `finally` Blocks
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**: Modify the program from Exercise 3 to include an `else` block that prints "Conversion successful!" if the number is successfully converted to an integer. Also, add a `finally` block that prints "Execution completed." regardless of whether an exception occurred or not.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                 | Points | Description                                                                                                   |
| ------------------------ | ------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| File Handling            | 2      | Program correctly opens and attempts to read from the file.                                                   |
| Try-Except Implementation | 3      | Program uses a `try-except` block to handle `FileNotFoundError` and `ValueError`.                             |
| Error Handling           | 3      | Program correctly catches both exceptions and prints appropriate messages.                                       |
| Else Block               | 1      | Program correctly implements and executes the `else` block when no exception occurs.                           |
| Finally Block            | 1      | Program correctly implements and executes the `finally` block regardless of exceptions.                         |

**Expected Answer Outline**:

```python
try:
    with open("numbers.txt", "r") as file:
        number_str = file.readline().strip()
        number = int(number_str)
except FileNotFoundError:
    print("Error: File not found.")
except ValueError:
    print("Error: Invalid content in the file. Please provide a valid integer.")
else:
    print("Conversion successful!")
    print("Number:", number)
finally:
    print("Execution completed.")
```

### Exercise 5: Raising Exceptions
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Advanced
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**: Write a function called `validate_age` that takes an age as input. If the age is less than 0 or greater than 120, raise a `ValueError` with an appropriate message. Otherwise, return the age. Write a program that uses this function and handles the potential `ValueError`.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                 | Points | Description                                                                                                   |
| ------------------------ | ------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Function Definition      | 3      | Function `validate_age` is correctly defined and takes an age as input.                                      |
| Exception Raising        | 4      | Function correctly raises a `ValueError` when the age is invalid.                                             |
| Program Implementation   | 3      | Program correctly calls the function and handles the potential `ValueError` using a `try-except` block.       |

**Expected Answer Outline**:

```python
def validate_age(age):
    if age < 0 or age > 120:
        raise ValueError("Invalid age. Age must be between 0 and 120.")
    return age

try:
    age = int(input("Enter your age: "))
    validated_age = validate_age(age)
    print("Age:", validated_age)
except ValueError as e:
    print("Error:", e)
```

### Exercise 6: Custom Exceptions
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Advanced
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**: Create a custom exception class called `InsufficientFundsError` that inherits from the `Exception` class. Write a program that simulates a bank account. The program should allow the user to deposit and withdraw money. If the user tries to withdraw more money than is available in the account, raise the `InsufficientFundsError`.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                 | Points | Description                                                                                                   |
| ------------------------ | ------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Custom Exception         | 3      | Custom exception class `InsufficientFundsError` is correctly defined.                                         |
| Program Implementation   | 5      | Program correctly implements deposit and withdrawal functionality.                                            |
| Exception Raising and Handling | 2      | Program correctly raises `InsufficientFundsError` and handles it appropriately.                               |

**Expected Answer Outline**:

```python
class InsufficientFundsError(Exception):
    pass

class BankAccount:
    def __init__(self, balance=0):
        self.balance = balance

    def deposit(self, amount):
        self.balance += amount
        print("Deposit successful. Current balance:", self.balance)

    def withdraw(self, amount):
        if amount > self.balance:
            raise InsufficientFundsError("Insufficient funds.")
        self.balance -= amount
        print("Withdrawal successful. Current balance:", self.balance)

account = BankAccount(100)

try:
    account.withdraw(150)
except InsufficientFundsError as e:
    print("Error:", e)

account.deposit(200)
account.withdraw(50)
```

# Introduction to OOP Concepts - Practice Materials

## Practice Exercises

### Exercise 1: Identify Objects
**Type**: Conceptual
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 10 minutes

**Instructions**:
Consider a simple online store. List five real-world objects that would be represented as objects in the software system. For each object, list three attributes (data) and three methods (actions).

**Solution Rubric**:
*   Correct identification of objects (2 points per object)
*   Appropriate attributes listed (1 point per attribute)
*   Appropriate methods listed (1 point per method)

### Exercise 2: Class Definition - Dog
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 15 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create a Python class called `Dog`. The class should have the following attributes: `name` (string), `breed` (string), and `age` (integer). It should also have a method called `bark()` that prints "Woof!" to the console.

**Solution Code**:
```python
class Dog:
    def __init__(self, name, breed, age):
        self.name = name
        self.breed = breed
        self.age = age

    def bark(self):
        print("Woof!")

# Example Usage
my_dog = Dog("Buddy", "Golden Retriever", 3)
print(my_dog.name)
my_dog.bark()
```

**Solution Rubric**:
*   Correct class definition (2 points)
*   Correct `__init__` method with attributes (3 points)
*   Correct `bark()` method (2 points)
*   Working example usage (3 points)

### Exercise 3: Inheritance - Animal and Cat
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create a class called `Animal`. It should have a method called `speak()` that prints "Generic animal sound." Create a class called `Cat` that inherits from `Animal`. Override the `speak()` method in the `Cat` class to print "Meow!".

**Solution Code**:
```python
class Animal:
    def speak(self):
        print("Generic animal sound")

class Cat(Animal):
    def speak(self):
        print("Meow!")

# Example Usage
my_animal = Animal()
my_cat = Cat()

my_animal.speak()
my_cat.speak()
```

**Solution Rubric**:
*   Correct `Animal` class definition (2 points)
*   Correct `speak()` method in `Animal` (1 point)
*   Correct `Cat` class definition inheriting from `Animal` (2 points)
*   Correct overriding of `speak()` method in `Cat` (3 points)
*   Working example usage (2 points)

### Exercise 4: Encapsulation - Bank Account
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create a class called `BankAccount`. It should have a private attribute called `__balance` (float).  It should have methods `deposit(amount)` and `withdraw(amount)` that update the balance.  The `withdraw` method should check if there is enough balance before withdrawing. Implement a `get_balance()` method that returns the current balance.

**Solution Code**:
```python
class BankAccount:
    def __init__(self, initial_balance=0.0):
        self.__balance = initial_balance

    def deposit(self, amount):
        if amount > 0:
            self.__balance += amount
            print(f"Deposited ${amount}. New balance: ${self.__balance}")
        else:
            print("Invalid deposit amount.")

    def withdraw(self, amount):
        if amount > 0 and amount <= self.__balance:
            self.__balance -= amount
            print(f"Withdrew ${amount}. New balance: ${self.__balance}")
        else:
            print("Insufficient balance or invalid withdrawal amount.")

    def get_balance(self):
        return self.__balance

# Example Usage
account = BankAccount(100.0)
account.deposit(50.0)
account.withdraw(20.0)
print(f"Current balance: ${account.get_balance()}")
account.withdraw(200.0)
```

**Solution Rubric**:
*   Correct private `__balance` attribute (2 points)
*   Correct `deposit()` method (3 points)
*   Correct `withdraw()` method with balance check (4 points)
*   Correct `get_balance()` method (1 point)

### Exercise 5: Polymorphism - Shape Classes
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Advanced
**Estimated Time**: 25 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create an abstract class called `Shape` with an abstract method called `area()`. Create two classes, `Rectangle` and `Circle`, that inherit from `Shape`. Implement the `area()` method for each class.  `Rectangle` should take `width` and `height` as input, and `Circle` should take `radius` as input.

**Solution Code**:
```python
from abc import ABC, abstractmethod
import math

class Shape(ABC):
    @abstractmethod
    def area(self):
        pass

class Rectangle(Shape):
    def __init__(self, width, height):
        self.width = width
        self.height = height

    def area(self):
        return self.width * self.height

class Circle(Shape):
    def __init__(self, radius):
        self.radius = radius

    def area(self):
        return math.pi * self.radius**2

# Example Usage
rect = Rectangle(5, 10)
circle = Circle(7)

print(f"Rectangle area: {rect.area()}")
print(f"Circle area: {circle.area()}")
```

**Solution Rubric**:
*   Correct abstract `Shape` class definition (2 points)
*   Correct abstract `area()` method in `Shape` (1 point)
*   Correct `Rectangle` class definition inheriting from `Shape` (2 points)
*   Correct `area()` method implementation in `Rectangle` (2 points)
*   Correct `Circle` class definition inheriting from `Shape` (2 points)
*   Correct `area()` method implementation in `Circle` (3 points)

### Exercise 6: Multiple Choice - OOP Concepts
**Type**: Multiple Choice
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 5 minutes

**Instructions**:
Choose the correct answer for each question.

1.  What is the primary purpose of encapsulation in OOP?
    A) To hide the implementation details of an object
    B) To allow objects of different classes to be treated as objects of a common type
    C) To create new classes from existing classes
    D) To define a common interface for multiple classes
    **Answer**: A

2.  Which OOP principle allows a class to inherit properties and methods from another class?
    A) Polymorphism
    B) Encapsulation
    C) Inheritance
    D) Abstraction
    **Answer**: C

3.  What is polymorphism in OOP?
    A) The ability of an object to take on many forms
    B) Hiding the implementation details of an object
    C) Creating new classes from existing classes
    D) Grouping related data and methods into a single unit
    **Answer**: A

### Exercise 6: Class Variables vs. Instance Variables
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create a class `BankAccount`. It should have a class variable `interest_rate` initialized to 0.02. It should have instance variables `account_number` and `balance`. Create methods to deposit, withdraw, and apply interest.

**Solution Rubric**:

# Methods and Attributes - Practice Materials

        self.name = name
        self.breed = breed

**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 15 minutes

**Instructions**:  Extend the `Dog` class from Exercise 2. Add a method called `bark` that prints "Woof!" to the console.

    def __init__(self, name, breed):
        self.name = name
        self.breed = breed

    def bark(self):
        print("Woof!")

# Example usage:
my_dog = Dog("Buddy", "Golden Retriever")
my_dog.bark() # Output: Woof!
```

### Exercise 4: Modifying Attributes
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 10 minutes

**Instructions**: Create a class `Car` with attributes `make`, `model`, and `speed` (initialized to 0). Add a method `accelerate(increment)` that increases the `speed` attribute by the given `increment`. Also, add a method `brake(decrement)` that decreases the `speed` attribute by the given `decrement`. Ensure the speed cannot be negative (if braking would result in negative speed, set speed to 0).

**Solution Rubric**:

*   Correct class definition: 2 points
*   Correct attribute initialization including speed=0: 3 points
*   Correct `accelerate` method: 3 points
*   Correct `brake` method with negative speed check: 7 points

```python
class Car:
    def __init__(self, make, model):
        self.make = make
        self.model = model
        self.speed = 0

    def accelerate(self, increment):
        self.speed += increment

    def brake(self, decrement):
        self.speed -= decrement
        if self.speed < 0:
            self.speed = 0

# Example usage:
my_car = Car("Toyota", "Camry")
my_car.accelerate(30)
print(my_car.speed) # Output: 30
my_car.brake(10)
print(my_car.speed) # Output: 20
my_car.brake(50)
print(my_car.speed) # Output: 0
```

### Exercise 5: Class Attributes vs. Instance Attributes
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 15 minutes

**Instructions**: Create a class `BankAccount`. It should have a class attribute `interest_rate` initialized to 0.02. The `__init__` method should take an `account_holder_name` and `balance` as arguments and set them as instance attributes. Add a method `apply_interest()` that increases the `balance` by the interest amount (balance * interest_rate).

**Solution Rubric**:

*   Correct class definition: 2 points
*   Correct class attribute definition: 3 points
*   Correct `__init__` method: 3 points
*   Correct `apply_interest` method: 7 points

```python
class BankAccount:
    interest_rate = 0.02  # Class attribute

    def __init__(self, account_holder_name, balance):
        self.account_holder_name = account_holder_name
        self.balance = balance

    def apply_interest(self):
        self.balance += self.balance * BankAccount.interest_rate #Accessing class attribute

# Example usage:
account1 = BankAccount("Alice", 1000)
account1.apply_interest()
print(account1.balance) # Output: 1020.0
```

A) The class itself.

*   Partial credit is not applicable.

### Exercise 7: Advanced Attribute Modification
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Advanced
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**: Create a class called `TemperatureSensor`.  It should have a private attribute `_temperature` (use name mangling with a single underscore). Implement getter and setter methods using the `@property` decorator for the `temperature` attribute. The setter should validate that the temperature is within a reasonable range (e.g., -50 to 100 degrees Celsius). If the temperature is outside this range, raise a `ValueError` with an appropriate message.

**Solution Rubric**:

*   Correct class definition: 2 points
*   Correct private attribute: 2 points
*   Correct getter method using `@property`: 5 points
*   Correct setter method using `@temperature.setter`: 5 points
*   Correct validation and `ValueError` handling: 6 points

```python
class TemperatureSensor:
    def __init__(self, initial_temperature=20):
        self._temperature = initial_temperature

    @property
    def temperature(self):
        return self._temperature

    @temperature.setter
    def temperature(self, new_temperature):
        if -50 <= new_temperature <= 100:
            self._temperature = new_temperature
        else:
            raise ValueError("Temperature out of range (-50 to 100 degrees Celsius)")

# Example usage:
sensor = TemperatureSensor()
print(sensor.temperature)  # Output: 20

try:
    sensor.temperature = 120
except ValueError as e:
    print(e) # Output: Temperature out of range (-50 to 100 degrees Celsius)

sensor.temperature = 25
print(sensor.temperature) # Output: 25
```

## Lesson 19

```markdown
# Inheritance - Practice Materials

## Learning Objectives

*   Understand the concept of inheritance in object-oriented programming.
*   Implement single, multiple, and multilevel inheritance in Python.
*   Use the `super()` function to access parent class methods and attributes.
*   Differentiate between method overriding and method overloading.
*   Apply inheritance to solve real-world programming problems.

## Practice Exercises

### Exercise 1: Basic Inheritance
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create a class `Animal` with attributes `name` and `species`. Add a method `make_sound()` that prints a generic animal sound (e.g., "Generic animal sound"). Then, create a class `Dog` that inherits from `Animal`.  Override the `make_sound()` method in the `Dog` class to print "Woof!". Create instances of both classes and call their `make_sound()` methods.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria          | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| ----------------- | ------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `Animal` Class    | 2      | Correctly defines the `Animal` class with `name`, `species` attributes and a `make_sound()` method.                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| `Dog` Class       | 3      | Correctly defines the `Dog` class inheriting from `Animal`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| Method Overriding | 3      | Correctly overrides the `make_sound()` method in the `Dog` class.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| Instantiation & Call | 2      | Correctly creates instances of both `Animal` and `Dog` classes and calls the `make_sound()` method on each.                                                                                                                                                                                           |

**Solution**:

```python
class Animal:
    def __init__(self, name, species):
        self.name = name
        self.species = species

    def make_sound(self):
        print("Generic animal sound")

class Dog(Animal):
    def __init__(self, name, breed):
        super().__init__(name, species="Dog") # Calling super class constructor
        self.breed = breed

    def make_sound(self):
        print("Woof!")

animal = Animal("Generic Animal", "Unknown")
dog = Dog("Buddy", "Golden Retriever")

animal.make_sound()
dog.make_sound()
```

### Exercise 2: Multiple Inheritance
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 30 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create two classes: `Swimmer` with a method `swim()` that prints "Swimming!" and `Runner` with a method `run()` that prints "Running!". Create a class `Athlete` that inherits from both `Swimmer` and `Runner`.  Create an instance of `Athlete` and call both `swim()` and `run()` methods.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria              | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                                        |
| --------------------- | ------ | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `Swimmer` Class       | 2      | Correctly defines the `Swimmer` class with the `swim()` method.                                                                                                                   |
| `Runner` Class        | 2      | Correctly defines the `Runner` class with the `run()` method.                                                                                                                    |
| `Athlete` Class       | 3      | Correctly defines the `Athlete` class inheriting from both `Swimmer` and `Runner`.                                                                                                |
| Method Calls          | 3      | Correctly creates an instance of the `Athlete` class and calls both `swim()` and `run()` methods.                                                                                  |

**Solution**:

```python
class Swimmer:
    def swim(self):
        print("Swimming!")

class Runner:
    def run(self):
        print("Running!")

class Athlete(Swimmer, Runner):
    pass

athlete = Athlete()
athlete.swim()
athlete.run()
```

### Exercise 3: Multilevel Inheritance
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 30 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create a class `Vehicle` with an attribute `engine_type`. Create a class `Car` that inherits from `Vehicle` and adds an attribute `model`. Create a class `ElectricCar` that inherits from `Car` and adds an attribute `battery_capacity`.  Create an instance of `ElectricCar` and print its `engine_type`, `model`, and `battery_capacity`.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria               | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| ---------------------- | ------ | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `Vehicle` Class        | 2      | Correctly defines the `Vehicle` class with the `engine_type` attribute.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| `Car` Class            | 3      | Correctly defines the `Car` class inheriting from `Vehicle` and adds the `model` attribute.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| `ElectricCar` Class    | 3      | Correctly defines the `ElectricCar` class inheriting from `Car` and adds the `battery_capacity` attribute.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| Attribute Access       | 2      | Correctly creates an instance of the `ElectricCar` class and prints the `engine_type`, `model`, and `battery_capacity` attributes.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |

**Solution**:

```python
class Vehicle:
    def __init__(self, engine_type):
        self.engine_type = engine_type

class Car(Vehicle):
    def __init__(self, engine_type, model):
        super().__init__(engine_type)
        self.model = model

class ElectricCar(Car):
    def __init__(self, model, battery_capacity):
        super().__init__("Electric", model)
        self.battery_capacity = battery_capacity

electric_car = ElectricCar("Model S", "100 kWh")
print(f"Engine Type: {electric_car.engine_type}")
print(f"Model: {electric_car.model}")
print(f"Battery Capacity: {electric_car.battery_capacity}")
```

### Exercise 4: The `super()` Function
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 25 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create a class `Rectangle` with attributes `length` and `width` and a method `area()` that calculates the area. Create a class `Square` that inherits from `Rectangle`. In the `Square` class, initialize both `length` and `width` to the same value using the `super()` function. Override the `area()` method in the `Square` class and ensure it calculates the area correctly.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria             | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| -------------------- | ------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| `Rectangle` Class    | 3      | Correctly defines the `Rectangle` class with `length` and `width` attributes and an `area()` method.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| `Square` Class       | 3      | Correctly defines the `Square` class inheriting from `Rectangle`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| `super()` Usage      | 2      | Correctly uses the `super()` function to initialize `length` and `width` in the `Square` class.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| Method Overriding & Correct Area Calculation | 2      | Correctly overrides the `area()` method in the `Square` class and calculates the area correctly.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |

**Solution**:

```python
class Rectangle:
    def __init__(self, length, width):
        self.length = length
        self.width = width

    def area(self):
        return self.length * self.width

class Square(Rectangle):
    def __init__(self, side):
        super().__init__(side, side)  # Call Rectangle's __init__ with side, side

    def area(self):
        return self.length * self.length

square = Square(5)
print(f"Area of square: {square.area()}")
```

### Exercise 5: Method Overriding and Polymorphism
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Advanced
**Estimated Time**: 35 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create a base class `Shape` with a method `draw()` that prints "Drawing a shape". Create three subclasses: `Circle`, `Rectangle`, and `Triangle`, each inheriting from `Shape`. Override the `draw()` method in each subclass to print "Drawing a circle", "Drawing a rectangle", and "Drawing a triangle", respectively. Create a list of `Shape` objects, including instances of the subclasses. Iterate through the list and call the `draw()` method on each object.  Demonstrate polymorphism.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| ----------------------- | ------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| `Shape` Class           | 2      | Correctly defines the `Shape` class with the `draw()` method.                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| Subclasses              | 3      | Correctly defines the `Circle`, `Rectangle`, and `Triangle` classes inheriting from `Shape`.                                                                                                                                                                   |
| Method Overriding       | 3      | Correctly overrides the `draw()` method in each subclass.                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| Polymorphism Demonstration | 2      | Correctly creates a list of `Shape` objects and demonstrates polymorphism by calling the `draw()` method on each object, resulting in the correct output for each shape.                                                                                           |

**Solution**:

```python
class Shape:
    def draw(self):
        print("Drawing a shape")

class Circle(Shape):
    def draw(self):
        print("Drawing a circle")

class Rectangle(Shape):
    def draw(self):
        print("Drawing a rectangle")

class Triangle(Shape):
    def draw(self):
        print("Drawing a triangle")

shapes = [Shape(), Circle(), Rectangle(), Triangle()]

for shape in shapes:
    shape.draw()
```

### Exercise 6:  Real-world scenario using inheritance
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 30 minutes

**Instructions**:
Design a system for managing bank accounts. Create a base class called `BankAccount` with attributes like `account_number`, `account_holder`, and `balance`. Include methods for depositing (`deposit()`) and withdrawing (`withdraw()`) money.  Create two subclasses: `SavingsAccount` and `CheckingAccount`. `SavingsAccount` should have an additional attribute `interest_rate` and a method `calculate_interest()`. `CheckingAccount` should have an attribute `transaction_limit` and a method to check if a withdrawal is within the limit.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                    | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| --------------------------- | ------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `BankAccount` Class         | 4      | Correctly defines the `BankAccount` class with the specified attributes and methods.  Handles basic deposit and withdrawal functionality.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| `SavingsAccount` Class      | 3      | Correctly defines the `SavingsAccount` class inheriting from `BankAccount` and includes the `interest_rate` attribute and `calculate_interest()` method.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| `CheckingAccount` Class     | 3      | Correctly defines the `CheckingAccount` class inheriting from `BankAccount` and includes the `transaction_limit` attribute and a method to check if a withdrawal is within the limit.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |

**Solution**:

```python
class BankAccount:
    def __init__(self, account_number, account_holder, balance=0):
        self.account_number = account_number
        self.account_holder = account_holder
        self.balance = balance

    def deposit(self, amount):
        self.balance += amount
        print(f"Deposited {amount}. New balance: {self.balance}")

    def withdraw(self, amount):
        if amount <= self.balance:
            self.balance -= amount
            print(f"Withdrew {amount}. New balance: {self.balance}")
        else:
            print("Insufficient funds.")

class SavingsAccount(BankAccount):
    def __init__(self, account_number, account_holder, interest_rate, balance=0):
        super().__init__(account_number, account_holder, balance)
        self.interest_rate = interest_rate

    def calculate_interest(self):
        interest = self.balance * self.interest_rate
        self.deposit(interest)
        print(f"Interest calculated and deposited: {interest}")

class CheckingAccount(BankAccount):
    def __init__(self, account_number, account_holder, transaction_limit, balance=0):
        super().__init__(account_number, account_holder, balance)
        self.transaction_limit = transaction_limit

    def withdraw(self, amount):
        if amount <= self.transaction_limit:
            super().withdraw(amount) # Calling the parent's withdraw method
        else:
            print("Withdrawal exceeds transaction limit.")

# Example Usage
savings_account = SavingsAccount("SA123", "Alice", 0.05, 1000)
savings_account.deposit(500)
savings_account.calculate_interest()

checking_account = CheckingAccount("CA456", "Bob", 200, 500)
checking_account.withdraw(100)
checking_account.withdraw(300) # Exceeds transaction limit
```

### Question 1

D) Reduced code duplication
**Answer**: B

### Question 2

### Question 3
What is method overriding?
A) Defining a method with the same name in a subclass as in its parent class.
B) Defining a method with a different name in a subclass.
C) Defining a method with the same name but different parameters in the same class.
D) Defining a method that cannot be accessed from outside the class.
**Answer**: A

### Question 4

A) Single inheritance
B) Multilevel inheritance
C) Multiple inheritance
D) Hierarchical inheritance
**Answer**: C

### Question 5

```python
class A:
    def display(self):
        print("A")

class B(A):
    def display(self):
        print("B")

obj = B()
obj.display()
```

What will be the output of the code?

A) A
B) B
C) A B
D) Error
**Answer**: B

**Assessment Criteria**:

| Criteria              | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| --------------------- | ------ | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |

| Method Overloading    | 6      | Accurately explains that Python doesn't directly support overloading and provides a valid alternative implementation (e.g., using default argument values or variable arguments) with a clear example.                                                                                                                                                    |

## Lesson 20

```markdown
# Polymorphism and Duck Typing - Practice Materials

## Practice Exercises

### Exercise 1: Polymorphic Calculation
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 15 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create a base class `Shape` with a method `calculate_area()` that returns 0.  Create two subclasses, `Rectangle` and `Circle`, that inherit from `Shape` and override the `calculate_area()` method to calculate the area of a rectangle and a circle, respectively.  Demonstrate polymorphism by creating a list of `Shape` objects (containing both `Rectangle` and `Circle` objects) and iterating through the list, calling `calculate_area()` on each object.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria | Points | Description |
|---|---|---|
| Correct `Shape` class definition | 2 | Base class defined with `calculate_area` returning 0. |
| Correct `Rectangle` class definition | 3 | `Rectangle` inherits from `Shape` and correctly calculates area. |
| Correct `Circle` class definition | 3 | `Circle` inherits from `Shape` and correctly calculates area. |
| Polymorphic iteration and output | 2 | Correctly iterates through the list and calls `calculate_area` on each object, producing the correct output. |

```python
import math

class Shape:
    def calculate_area(self):
        return 0

class Rectangle(Shape):
    def __init__(self, width, height):
        self.width = width
        self.height = height

    def calculate_area(self):
        return self.width * self.height

class Circle(Shape):
    def __init__(self, radius):
        self.radius = radius

    def calculate_area(self):
        return math.pi * self.radius**2

shapes = [Rectangle(5, 10), Circle(7), Rectangle(3, 4)]

for shape in shapes:
    print(f"Area: {shape.calculate_area()}")
```

### Exercise 2: Duck Typing with a `Quack` Method
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create two classes, `Duck` and `Person`. The `Duck` class should have a `quack()` method that prints "Quack!". The `Person` class should have a `quack()` method that prints "The person imitates a duck: Quack!". Create a function called `make_it_quack()` that takes any object as input and calls its `quack()` method. Demonstrate duck typing by calling `make_it_quack()` with instances of both the `Duck` and `Person` classes.  Also, attempt to call `make_it_quack()` with an object that *doesn't* have a `quack()` method and handle the resulting error gracefully using a `try-except` block.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria | Points | Description |
|---|---|---|
| Correct `Duck` class definition | 2 | `Duck` class with a `quack()` method. |
| Correct `Person` class definition | 2 | `Person` class with a `quack()` method. |
| Correct `make_it_quack` function definition | 3 | Function takes any object and calls `quack()` |
| Demonstration of duck typing | 2 | Correctly calls `make_it_quack` with instances of `Duck` and `Person`. |
| Error handling | 1 | Correctly handles the `AttributeError` when an object without a `quack()` method is passed to `make_it_quack`. |

```python
class Duck:
    def quack(self):
        print("Quack!")

class Person:
    def quack(self):
        print("The person imitates a duck: Quack!")

def make_it_quack(obj):
    try:
        obj.quack()
    except AttributeError:
        print("This object cannot quack!")

duck = Duck()
person = Person()
integer = 5

make_it_quack(duck)
make_it_quack(person)
make_it_quack(integer)
```

### Exercise 3: Polymorphism with File Handling
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 25 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create a base class `FileProcessor` with a method `process_file(filename)` that reads the content of a file. Create two subclasses, `TextFileProcessor` and `BinaryFileProcessor`. `TextFileProcessor` should read the file as text and print each line. `BinaryFileProcessor` should read the file as binary and print the hexadecimal representation of the first 16 bytes. Demonstrate polymorphism by creating a function that takes a `FileProcessor` object and a filename as input and calls the `process_file()` method. Test this function with both `TextFileProcessor` and `BinaryFileProcessor` objects, using appropriate file types (e.g., a `.txt` file and a `.bin` file or a `.jpg` file). You can create small dummy files for testing.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria | Points | Description |
|---|---|---|
| Correct `FileProcessor` class definition | 2 | Base class defined with `process_file`. |
| Correct `TextFileProcessor` class definition | 3 | Reads and prints a text file line by line. |
| Correct `BinaryFileProcessor` class definition | 3 | Reads and prints the hexadecimal representation of the first 16 bytes of a binary file. |
| Polymorphic function and output | 2 | Correctly implements the function and produces the expected output for both file types. |

```python
class FileProcessor:
    def process_file(self, filename):
        pass

class TextFileProcessor(FileProcessor):
    def process_file(self, filename):
        try:
            with open(filename, 'r') as f:
                for line in f:
                    print(line.strip())
        except FileNotFoundError:
            print(f"Error: File '{filename}' not found.")

class BinaryFileProcessor(FileProcessor):
    def process_file(self, filename):
        try:
            with open(filename, 'rb') as f:
                content = f.read(16)
                print(" ".join([f"{byte:02x}" for byte in content]))
        except FileNotFoundError:
            print(f"Error: File '{filename}' not found.")

def process_the_file(processor, filename):
    processor.process_file(filename)

# Example Usage (assuming you have text.txt and binary.bin files)
text_processor = TextFileProcessor()
binary_processor = BinaryFileProcessor()

#Create dummy test files
with open("text.txt", "w") as f:
    f.write("This is a test text file.\n")
    f.write("It has two lines.")

with open("binary.bin", "wb") as f:
    f.write(bytes([0x01, 0x02, 0x03, 0x04, 0x05, 0x06, 0x07, 0x08, 0x09, 0x0A, 0x0B, 0x0C, 0x0D, 0x0E, 0x0F, 0x10]))


process_the_file(text_processor, "text.txt")
process_the_file(binary_processor, "binary.bin")
```

### Exercise 4: Advanced Duck Typing - The `Moveable` Interface
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Advanced
**Estimated Time**: 30 minutes

**Instructions**:
Imagine you're building a game.  You want different objects (cars, birds, planes) to be able to `move()`.  Instead of using inheritance, leverage duck typing.  Create classes `Car`, `Bird`, and `Plane`.  Each class should have a `move()` method that prints a specific message indicating how that object moves (e.g., "The car drives down the road.", "The bird flies through the air.", "The plane soars through the sky.").  Create a function `move_all(objects)` that takes a list of objects as input and calls the `move()` method on each object in the list.  Demonstrate that the function works correctly, and then add a `Rock` class that *doesn't* have a `move()` method.  Handle the potential `AttributeError` in the `move_all` function gracefully, printing an informative error message if an object in the list doesn't have a `move()` method.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria | Points | Description |
|---|---|---|
| Correct `Car`, `Bird`, `Plane` class definitions | 4 | Each class has a `move()` method that prints the correct message. |
| Correct `move_all` function definition | 3 | Function iterates through the list and calls `move()` on each object. |
| Demonstration of duck typing | 2 | Correctly calls `move_all` with instances of `Car`, `Bird`, and `Plane`. |
| Error handling | 1 | Correctly handles the `AttributeError` when the `Rock` object is included. |

```python
class Car:
    def move(self):
        print("The car drives down the road.")

class Bird:
    def move(self):
        print("The bird flies through the air.")

class Plane:
    def move(self):
        print("The plane soars through the sky.")

class Rock: # No move method
    pass

def move_all(objects):
    for obj in objects:
        try:
            obj.move()
        except AttributeError:
            print(f"Error: Object of type {type(obj).__name__} cannot move.")

objects = [Car(), Bird(), Plane(), Rock()]
move_all(objects)
```

# Encapsulation and Abstraction - Practice Materials

## Practice Exercises

### Exercise 1: Identifying Encapsulation
**Type**: Multiple Choice
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 5 minutes

**Instructions**:
Which of the following best describes encapsulation in object-oriented programming?

A) Hiding the internal implementation details of an object and exposing only what is necessary.
B) Inheriting properties and methods from a parent class.
C) Creating multiple objects from the same class.
D) Defining the structure of a class.

**Solution Rubric**:
A) Correct (1 point)
Other options: Incorrect (0 points)

### Exercise 2: Creating a Simple Class with Encapsulation
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 15 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create a `BankAccount` class with the following attributes: `account_number` (private), `account_holder_name` (private), and `balance` (private). Include methods to deposit, withdraw, and get the balance. Ensure that the balance cannot be directly modified from outside the class.

**Solution Rubric**:
- Correct class structure with private attributes (5 points)
- Correct `deposit` method (3 points)
- Correct `withdraw` method (3 points)
- Correct `get_balance` method (2 points)
- Balance not directly modifiable (2 points)

```python
class BankAccount:
    def __init__(self, account_number, account_holder_name, initial_balance=0):
        self.__account_number = account_number  # Private attribute
        self.__account_holder_name = account_holder_name #Private attribute
        self.__balance = initial_balance  # Private attribute

    def deposit(self, amount):
        if amount > 0:
            self.__balance += amount
            return True
        else:
            return False

    def withdraw(self, amount):
        if 0 < amount <= self.__balance:
            self.__balance -= amount
            return True
        else:
            return False

    def get_balance(self):
        return self.__balance

    def get_account_number(self):
        return self.__account_number

    def get_account_holder_name(self):
        return self.__account_holder_name

#Example usage
account = BankAccount("123456789", "John Doe", 1000)
account.deposit(500)
account.withdraw(200)
print(account.get_balance()) #Output: 1300
```

### Exercise 3: Understanding Abstraction
**Type**: Essay
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**:
Explain the concept of abstraction in object-oriented programming. Provide an example of how abstraction can be used in a real-world scenario.

**Solution Rubric**:
- Clear definition of abstraction (5 points)
- Explanation of how it simplifies complex systems (5 points)
- Relevant real-world example (5 points)

### Exercise 4: Implementing Abstraction with Abstract Classes
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Advanced
**Estimated Time**: 25 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create an abstract class called `Shape` with an abstract method `area()`. Create two concrete classes, `Rectangle` and `Circle`, that inherit from `Shape` and implement the `area()` method.

**Solution Rubric**:
- Correct abstract class definition (5 points)
- Correct abstract method definition (3 points)
- Correct `Rectangle` class implementation (4 points)
- Correct `Circle` class implementation (4 points)
```python
from abc import ABC, abstractmethod
import math

class Shape(ABC):
    @abstractmethod
    def area(self):
        pass

class Rectangle(Shape):
    def __init__(self, length, width):
        self.length = length
        self.width = width

    def area(self):
        return self.length * self.width

class Circle(Shape):
    def __init__(self, radius):
        self.radius = radius

    def area(self):
        return math.pi * self.radius**2

# Example usage
rect = Rectangle(5, 10)
circ = Circle(7)

print(rect.area()) # Output: 50
print(circ.area()) # Output: 153.93804002589985
```

### Exercise 5: Benefits of Encapsulation and Abstraction
**Type**: Multiple Choice
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 5 minutes

**Instructions**:
Which of the following is a primary benefit of using encapsulation and abstraction?

A) Increased code complexity
B) Reduced code reusability
C) Improved code maintainability and reduced dependencies
D) Decreased flexibility in code design

**Solution Rubric**:
C) Correct (1 point)
Other options: Incorrect (0 points)

### Exercise 6: Applying Encapsulation to a Data Class
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 15 minutes

**Instructions**:
Create a `Student` class with `name` (private), `student_id` (private) and `grades` (private list). Provide methods to add a grade, calculate the average grade, and get the student's name and ID. Prevent direct access to the `grades` list from outside the class.

**Solution Rubric**:
- Correct class structure with private attributes (5 points)
- Correct `add_grade` method (3 points)
- Correct `calculate_average_grade` method (4 points)
- Correct getter methods for name and ID (2 points)
```python
class Student:
    def __init__(self, name, student_id):
        self.__name = name
        self.__student_id = student_id
        self.__grades = []

    def add_grade(self, grade):
        if 0 <= grade <= 100:
            self.__grades.append(grade)

    def calculate_average_grade(self):
        if not self.__grades:
            return 0
        return sum(self.__grades) / len(self.__grades)

    def get_name(self):
        return self.__name

    def get_student_id(self):
        return self.__student_id

# Example usage
student = Student("Alice", "12345")
student.add_grade(85)
student.add_grade(92)
print(student.calculate_average_grade()) # Output: 88.5
print(student.get_name()) # Output: Alice
```

# Opening and Closing Files - Practice Materials

## Practice Exercises

### Exercise 1: File Opening Modes

    B)  `a+`
    C)  `w`

### Exercise 2: Opening and Closing a File
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 10 minutes

**Instructions**: Write a Python program to open a file named "my_file.txt" in read mode, print the first line, and then close the file.  Assume "my_file.txt" exists and contains at least one line.

| Criteria             | Points |

| Closes file          | 1      |

| **Total**            | **6**  |

**Expected Answer:**

```python
try:
    file = open("my_file.txt", "r")
    first_line = file.readline()
    print(first_line)
    file.close()
except FileNotFoundError:
    print("File not found.")
except Exception as e:
    print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
```

### Exercise 4: Appending to a File
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 10 minutes

**Instructions**: Write a Python program to open an existing file named "my_file.txt" in append mode (`a`). Add the line "This line is appended.\n" to the end of the file. Then close the file.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                       | Points |
| ------------------------------ | ------ |
| Correctly opens file in append mode | 2      |
| Appends the line               | 3      |
| Closes file                    | 2      |
| Code runs                     | 3      |
| **Total**                      | **10** |

**Expected Answer:**

```python
try:
    file = open("my_file.txt", "a")
    file.write("This line is appended.\n")
    file.close()
    print("Line appended successfully.")
except FileNotFoundError:
    print("File not found.")
except Exception as e:
    print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
```

### Exercise 5: Using `with` statement
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 10 minutes

**Instructions**: Rewrite Exercise 2 using the `with` statement for automatic file closing.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                       | Points |
| ------------------------------ | ------ |

| Correctly opens file          | 1      |
| Reads and prints the line     | 3      |
| Code runs                     | 3      |
| **Total**                      | **10** |

**Expected Answer:**

```python
try:
    with open("my_file.txt", "r") as file:
        first_line = file.readline()
        print(first_line)
except FileNotFoundError:
    print("File not found.")
except Exception as e:
    print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
```

### Exercise 6: Handling File Not Found Error
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 10 minutes

**Instructions**: Write a Python program that attempts to open a file named "nonexistent_file.txt" in read mode.  If the file does not exist, catch the `FileNotFoundError` exception and print "File not found!".

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                       | Points |
| ------------------------------ | ------ |
| Attempts to open nonexistent file | 2      |
| Catches `FileNotFoundError`     | 4      |
| Prints "File not found!"       | 2      |
| Code runs                     | 2      |
| **Total**                      | **10** |

**Expected Answer:**

```python
try:
    file = open("nonexistent_file.txt", "r")
    file.close() # This line will not be reached if the file is not found.
except FileNotFoundError:
    print("File not found!")
except Exception as e:
    print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
```

### Exercise 7: Reading all lines from a file
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 15 minutes

**Instructions**: Write a Python program that opens the file "my_file.txt" in read mode and prints each line of the file. Handle the `FileNotFoundError` exception.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                       | Points |
| ------------------------------ | ------ |
| Opens file correctly           | 2      |
| Reads all lines                | 4      |
| Prints each line               | 2      |
| Handles FileNotFoundError      | 2      |
| **Total**                      | **10** |

**Expected Answer:**

```python
try:
    with open("my_file.txt", "r") as file:
        for line in file:
            print(line, end="") # end="" prevents double spacing
except FileNotFoundError:
    print("File not found!")
except Exception as e:
    print(f"An error occurred: {e}")
```

A) To write data to a file.
B) To read data from a file.
C) To release system resources used by the file.
D) To rename a file.
**Answer**: C

A) `file.close()`

D) Both B and C
**Answer**: D

## Lesson 23

```markdown
# Reading and Writing Files - Practice Materials

## Practice Exercises

### Exercise 1: Simple File Reading
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 10 minutes

**Instructions**:
1. Create a text file named `my_file.txt` with the following content:
   ```
   This is the first line.
   This is the second line.
   This is the third line.
   ```
2. Write a Python program to open `my_file.txt` and print each line to the console.

**Solution Rubric**:
*   Correctly opens the file (2 points)
*   Reads and prints each line without errors (5 points)
*   Properly closes the file (3 points)

```python
# Solution
file = open("my_file.txt", "r")
for line in file:
    print(line.strip()) # .strip() removes newline characters
file.close()
```

### Exercise 2: Writing to a File
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 10 minutes

**Instructions**:
1. Write a Python program that prompts the user to enter three lines of text.
2. Write these lines to a new file named `user_input.txt`.

**Solution Rubric**:
*   Correctly prompts the user for input (3 points)
*   Opens the file in write mode (2 points)
*   Writes the user input to the file (5 points)

```python
# Solution
file = open("user_input.txt", "w")
for i in range(3):
    line = input("Enter line " + str(i+1) + ": ")
    file.write(line + "\n")  # Add newline character
file.close()
```

### Exercise 3: Appending to a File
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 10 minutes

**Instructions**:
1.  Using the `user_input.txt` file created in Exercise 2, write a Python program to append the line "This line was appended." to the end of the file.

**Solution Rubric**:
*   Opens the file in append mode (5 points)
*   Appends the correct line to the file (5 points)

```python
# Solution
file = open("user_input.txt", "a")
file.write("This line was appended.\n")
file.close()
```

### Exercise 4: Reading a File into a List
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 15 minutes

**Instructions**:
1.  Write a Python program that reads the contents of `my_file.txt` into a list, where each element of the list is a line from the file.
2.  Print the list to the console.

**Solution Rubric**:
*   Correctly opens the file (2 points)
*   Reads each line into a list (6 points)
*   Prints the list correctly (2 points)

```python
# Solution
file = open("my_file.txt", "r")
lines = file.readlines()
file.close()
print(lines)
```

### Exercise 5: Counting Words in a File
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**:
1.  Write a Python program that reads the `user_input.txt` file and counts the number of words in the file.
2.  Print the word count to the console.
    *   Hint: Use the `split()` method.

**Solution Rubric**:
*   Correctly opens the file (2 points)
*   Reads the file contents (2 points)
*   Splits the contents into words (3 points)
*   Counts the words correctly (3 points)

```python
# Solution
file = open("user_input.txt", "r")
content = file.read()
file.close()
words = content.split()
word_count = len(words)
print("Word count:", word_count)
```

### Exercise 6: Handling File Not Found Exceptions
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 10 minutes

**Instructions**:
1. Write a Python program that attempts to open a file named `non_existent_file.txt`.
2. Use a `try-except` block to catch the `FileNotFoundError` and print an appropriate error message if the file does not exist.

**Solution Rubric**:
*   Uses a `try-except` block (5 points)
*   Correctly catches the `FileNotFoundError` (3 points)
*   Prints an appropriate error message (2 points)

```python
# Solution
try:
    file = open("non_existent_file.txt", "r")
    content = file.read()
    file.close()
    print(content)
except FileNotFoundError:
    print("Error: File not found.")
```

### Exercise 7: Reading and Writing Binary Files (Optional)
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Advanced
**Estimated Time**: 25 minutes

**Instructions**:
1.  Create a byte array of size 256, containing integers from 0 to 255.
2.  Write this byte array to a binary file named `binary_data.bin`.
3.  Read the binary file back and print the first 10 bytes.

**Solution Rubric**:
*   Creates the byte array correctly (3 points)
*   Writes the byte array to a binary file (4 points)
*   Reads the binary file correctly (4 points)
*   Prints the first 10 bytes correctly (4 points)

```python
# Solution
data = bytearray(range(256))

# Writing to binary file
with open("binary_data.bin", "wb") as file:
    file.write(bytes(data))

# Reading from binary file
with open("binary_data.bin", "rb") as file:
    read_data = file.read(10)
    print(read_data)
```

A) "r"
B) "a"
C) "w"
D) "x"
**Answer**: C

### Question 2

A) IOError
B) ValueError
C) FileNotFoundError
D) TypeError
**Answer**: C

### Question 3

A) `read()`
B) `readline()`
C) `readlines()`
D) `readall()`
**Answer**: C

### Question 4

A) To remove leading spaces only.
B) To remove trailing spaces only.
C) To remove leading and trailing whitespace characters, including newline characters.

**Answer**: C
