## Lesson 24

```markdown
# Working with CSV Files - Practice Materials

## Learning Objectives

*   Understand the structure of CSV files.
*   Learn how to read data from CSV files using Python's `csv` module.
*   Learn how to write data to CSV files using Python's `csv` module.
*   Handle different CSV dialects and delimiters.
*   Perform data manipulation and analysis with CSV data.

## Practice Exercises

### Exercise 1: Reading a Simple CSV File
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 15 minutes

**Instructions**:
1.  Create a CSV file named `students.csv` with the following data:

    ```csv
    Name,Age,Major
    Alice,20,Computer Science
    Bob,22,Electrical Engineering
    Charlie,21,Mechanical Engineering
    ```

2.  Write a Python program to read the data from `students.csv` and print each row.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                 | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| ------------------------ | ------ | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Correct file opening     | 2      | The program correctly opens the `students.csv` file in read mode.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| CSV reader instantiation | 2      | The program correctly creates a `csv.reader` object.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| Row iteration            | 3      | The program iterates through each row in the CSV file.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| Output correctness       | 3      | The program correctly prints each row of data.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| **Total**                | **10** |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |

**Expected Answer**:

```python
import csv

with open('students.csv', 'r') as file:
    reader = csv.reader(file)
    for row in reader:
        print(row)
```

### Exercise 2: Reading CSV with Header
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 15 minutes

**Instructions**:
1.  Using the same `students.csv` file from Exercise 1, write a Python program to read the data and print each student's name and major. Use the header row to identify the columns.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                 | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| ------------------------ | ------ | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Correct file opening     | 2      | The program correctly opens the `students.csv` file in read mode.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| CSV reader instantiation | 2      | The program correctly creates a `csv.reader` object.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| Header extraction        | 2      | The program correctly extracts the header row.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| Data extraction          | 2      | The program correctly extracts the name and major from each row.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| Output correctness       | 2      | The program correctly prints the name and major for each student.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| **Total**                | **10** |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |

**Expected Answer**:

```python
import csv

with open('students.csv', 'r') as file:
    reader = csv.reader(file)
    header = next(reader)  # Skip the header row
    for row in reader:
        name = row[0]
        major = row[2]
        print(f"Name: {name}, Major: {major}")
```

### Exercise 3: Writing to a CSV File
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**:
1.  Write a Python program that creates a new CSV file named `courses.csv` and writes the following data to it:

    ```csv
    Course,Credits,Instructor
    Data Structures,3,Dr. Smith
    Algorithms,4,Prof. Johnson
    Operating Systems,3,Dr. Brown
    ```

2.  Ensure that the program handles the file opening and writing operations correctly.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                 | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| ------------------------ | ------ | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Correct file opening     | 2      | The program correctly opens the `courses.csv` file in write mode.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| CSV writer instantiation | 2      | The program correctly creates a `csv.writer` object.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| Header writing           | 2      | The program correctly writes the header row.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| Data writing             | 3      | The program correctly writes the data rows to the CSV file.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| File closure             | 1      | The program ensures that the file is properly closed after writing.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| **Total**                | **10** |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |

**Expected Answer**:

```python
import csv

with open('courses.csv', 'w', newline='') as file:
    writer = csv.writer(file)
    writer.writerow(['Course', 'Credits', 'Instructor'])
    writer.writerow(['Data Structures', '3', 'Dr. Smith'])
    writer.writerow(['Algorithms', '4', 'Prof. Johnson'])
    writer.writerow(['Operating Systems', '3', 'Dr. Brown'])
```

### Exercise 4: Using `csv.DictReader`
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**:
1.  Using the `students.csv` file from Exercise 1, write a Python program to read the data using `csv.DictReader` and print each student's name and age.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                 | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| ------------------------ | ------ | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Correct file opening     | 2      | The program correctly opens the `students.csv` file in read mode.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| DictReader instantiation | 2      | The program correctly creates a `csv.DictReader` object.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| Row iteration            | 3      | The program iterates through each row in the CSV file.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| Data access              | 2      | The program correctly accesses the name and age from each row using the dictionary keys.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| Output correctness       | 1      | The program correctly prints the name and age for each student.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| **Total**                | **10** |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |

**Expected Answer**:

```python
import csv

with open('students.csv', 'r') as file:
    reader = csv.DictReader(file)
    for row in reader:
        name = row['Name']
        age = row['Age']
        print(f"Name: {name}, Age: {age}")
```

### Exercise 5: Using `csv.DictWriter`
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**:
1.  Write a Python program that creates a new CSV file named `professors.csv` and writes the following data to it using `csv.DictWriter`:

    ```python
    data = [
        {'Name': 'Dr. Smith', 'Department': 'Computer Science', 'Rank': 'Professor'},
        {'Name': 'Prof. Johnson', 'Department': 'Electrical Engineering', 'Rank': 'Associate Professor'},
        {'Name': 'Dr. Brown', 'Department': 'Mechanical Engineering', 'Rank': 'Assistant Professor'}
    ]
    ```

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                 | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| ------------------------ | ------ | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Correct file opening     | 2      | The program correctly opens the `professors.csv` file in write mode.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| DictWriter instantiation | 2      | The program correctly creates a `csv.DictWriter` object.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| Header writing           | 2      | The program correctly writes the header row.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| Data writing             | 3      | The program correctly writes the data rows to the CSV file.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| File closure             | 1      | The program ensures that the file is properly closed after writing.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| **Total**                | **10** |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |

**Expected Answer**:

```python
import csv

data = [
    {'Name': 'Dr. Smith', 'Department': 'Computer Science', 'Rank': 'Professor'},
    {'Name': 'Prof. Johnson', 'Department': 'Electrical Engineering', 'Rank': 'Associate Professor'},
    {'Name': 'Dr. Brown', 'Department': 'Mechanical Engineering', 'Rank': 'Assistant Professor'}
]

with open('professors.csv', 'w', newline='') as file:
    fieldnames = ['Name', 'Department', 'Rank']
    writer = csv.DictWriter(file, fieldnames=fieldnames)
    writer.writeheader()
    writer.writerows(data)
```

### Exercise 6: Handling Different Delimiters
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Advanced
**Estimated Time**: 25 minutes

**Instructions**:
1.  Create a file named `data.txt` with the following data, using a semicolon (`;`) as the delimiter:

    ```txt
    Name;Age;Major
    Alice;20;Computer Science
    Bob;22;Electrical Engineering
    Charlie;21;Mechanical Engineering
    ```

2.  Write a Python program to read the data from `data.txt` and print each student's name and major.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria                 | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| ------------------------ | ------ | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Correct file opening     | 2      | The program correctly opens the `data.txt` file in read mode.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| CSV reader instantiation | 3      | The program correctly creates a `csv.reader` object with the correct delimiter specified.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| Row iteration            | 2      | The program iterates through each row in the file.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| Data extraction          | 2      | The program correctly extracts the name and major from each row.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| Output correctness       | 1      | The program correctly prints the name and major for each student.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| **Total**                | **10** |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |

**Expected Answer**:

```python
import csv

with open('data.txt', 'r') as file:
    reader = csv.reader(file, delimiter=';')
    header = next(reader)  # Skip the header row
    for row in reader:
        name = row[0]
        major = row[2]
        print(f"Name: {name}, Major: {major}")
```

## Lesson 25

```markdown
# Introduction to Testing Concepts - Practice Materials

## Practice Exercises

### Exercise 1: What is Unit Testing?
**Type**: Multiple Choice
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 5 minutes

**Instructions**:
Choose the best definition of unit testing.

A) Testing the entire application as a whole.
B) Testing individual components or functions in isolation.
C) Testing the user interface of the application.
D) Testing the performance of the application under heavy load.

**Answer**: B

### Exercise 2: Benefits of Testing
**Type**: Multiple Choice
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 5 minutes

**Instructions**:
Which of the following is NOT a benefit of writing tests?

A) Early detection of bugs.
B) Improved code maintainability.
C) Increased development time.
D) Enhanced code reliability.

**Answer**: C

### Exercise 3: Writing a Simple Unit Test
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 15 minutes

**Instructions**:
Write a unit test for the following function using the `unittest` module:

```python
def add(x, y):
  """Adds two numbers together."""
  return x + y
```

**Solution Rubric**:
- Correctly imports the `unittest` module. (2 points)
- Defines a test class that inherits from `unittest.TestCase`. (3 points)
- Creates a test method (e.g., `test_add`) that calls the `add` function. (3 points)
- Uses `self.assertEqual` or similar assertion method to verify the result. (2 points)

**Example Solution**:

```python
import unittest

def add(x, y):
  """Adds two numbers together."""
  return x + y

class TestAdd(unittest.TestCase):
  def test_add_positive_numbers(self):
    self.assertEqual(add(2, 3), 5)

  def test_add_negative_numbers(self):
    self.assertEqual(add(-2, -3), -5)

  def test_add_mixed_numbers(self):
    self.assertEqual(add(2, -3), -1)

if __name__ == '__main__':
  unittest.main()
```

**Type**: Multiple Choice
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 5 minutes

What is the primary difference between unit testing and integration testing?

A) Unit testing tests the entire application, while integration testing tests individual components.
B) Unit testing tests individual components, while integration testing tests how components interact with each other.
C) Unit testing focuses on performance, while integration testing focuses on functionality.
D) There is no difference between unit testing and integration testing.

**Answer**: B

### Exercise 8: Writing a Test Suite
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 10 minutes

**Instructions**:
Given the following test classes, create a test suite to run both sets of tests:

```python
import unittest

class TestAdd(unittest.TestCase):
  def test_add_positive_numbers(self):
    self.assertEqual(2 + 3, 5)

class TestSubtract(unittest.TestCase):
  def test_subtract_positive_numbers(self):
    self.assertEqual(5 - 2, 3)
```

**Solution Rubric**:
- Correctly creates a `TestSuite` object. (3 points)
- Adds both test classes or individual tests to the suite. (4 points)
- Runs the test suite using `unittest.TextTestRunner`. (3 points)

**Example Solution**:

```python
import unittest

class TestAdd(unittest.TestCase):
  def test_add_positive_numbers(self):
    self.assertEqual(2 + 3, 5)

class TestSubtract(unittest.TestCase):
  def test_subtract_positive_numbers(self):
    self.assertEqual(5 - 2, 3)

if __name__ == '__main__':
  suite = unittest.TestSuite()
  suite.addTest(unittest.makeSuite(TestAdd))
  suite.addTest(unittest.makeSuite(TestSubtract))

  runner = unittest.TextTestRunner()
  runner.run(suite)
```

# Unit Testing with `unittest` - Practice Materials

## Practice Exercises

### Exercise 1: Basic Test Case Creation
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 15 minutes

**Instructions**:
1. Create a Python function called `add(x, y)` that returns the sum of two numbers.
2. Create a `unittest.TestCase` class called `TestAdd`.
3. Within `TestAdd`, write a test method called `test_add_positive` that asserts that `add(2, 3)` returns 5.
4. Run the test using `unittest.main()`.

**Solution Rubric**:
- Correct `add(x, y)` function (2 points)
- Correct `TestAdd` class and setup (2 points)
- Correct `test_add_positive` method with assertion (4 points)
- Test runs successfully (2 points)

```python
import unittest

def add(x, y):
    return x + y

class TestAdd(unittest.TestCase):
    def test_add_positive(self):
        self.assertEqual(add(2, 3), 5)

if __name__ == '__main__':
    unittest.main()
```

### Exercise 2: Testing Different Data Types
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**:
1. Modify the `add(x, y)` function to handle floating-point numbers.
2. Add the following test methods to the `TestAdd` class:
    - `test_add_negative`: Assert that `add(-1, -2)` returns -3.
    - `test_add_float`: Assert that `add(1.5, 2.5)` returns 4.0.
3. Run the tests.

**Solution Rubric**:
- `add(x, y)` function correctly handles floats and negatives (3 points)
- `test_add_negative` method with assertion (3 points)
- `test_add_float` method with assertion (3 points)
- All tests run successfully (1 point)

```python
import unittest

def add(x, y):
    return x + y

class TestAdd(unittest.TestCase):
    def test_add_positive(self):
        self.assertEqual(add(2, 3), 5)

    def test_add_negative(self):
        self.assertEqual(add(-1, -2), -3)

    def test_add_float(self):
        self.assertEqual(add(1.5, 2.5), 4.0)

if __name__ == '__main__':
    unittest.main()
```

### Exercise 3: Testing Edge Cases and Error Handling
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Advanced
**Estimated Time**: 25 minutes

**Instructions**:
1. Modify the `add(x, y)` function to raise a `TypeError` if either `x` or `y` is not a number (int or float).
2. Add a test method called `test_add_invalid_input` to the `TestAdd` class that uses `assertRaises` to assert that `add("a", 2)` raises a `TypeError`.
3. Add a test method called `test_add_zero` to assert that `add(0, 5)` returns 5.

**Solution Rubric**:
- `add(x, y)` function correctly raises `TypeError` (4 points)
- `test_add_invalid_input` method with `assertRaises` (4 points)
- `test_add_zero` method with assertion (1 point)
- All tests run successfully (1 point)

```python
import unittest

def add(x, y):
    if not isinstance(x, (int, float)) or not isinstance(y, (int, float)):
        raise TypeError("Inputs must be numbers")
    return x + y

class TestAdd(unittest.TestCase):
    def test_add_positive(self):
        self.assertEqual(add(2, 3), 5)

    def test_add_negative(self):
        self.assertEqual(add(-1, -2), -3)

    def test_add_float(self):
        self.assertEqual(add(1.5, 2.5), 4.0)

    def test_add_invalid_input(self):
        with self.assertRaises(TypeError):
            add("a", 2)

    def test_add_zero(self):
        self.assertEqual(add(0, 5), 5)


if __name__ == '__main__':
    unittest.main()
```

### Exercise 4: Testing a Class Method
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**:
1. Create a class `Calculator` with a method `multiply(x, y)` that returns the product of two numbers.
2. Create a `unittest.TestCase` class called `TestCalculator`.
3. Write a test method called `test_multiply_positive` that asserts that `Calculator().multiply(2, 3)` returns 6.
4. Write test methods for negative and floating-point numbers.

**Solution Rubric**:
- Correct `Calculator` class and `multiply` method (3 points)
- Correct `TestCalculator` class setup (2 points)
- Correct `test_multiply_positive` method with assertion (2 points)
- Test methods for negative and floating-point numbers (2 points)
- All tests run successfully (1 point)

```python
import unittest

class Calculator:
    def multiply(self, x, y):
        return x * y

class TestCalculator(unittest.TestCase):
    def test_multiply_positive(self):
        self.assertEqual(Calculator().multiply(2, 3), 6)

    def test_multiply_negative(self):
        self.assertEqual(Calculator().multiply(-2, 3), -6)

    def test_multiply_float(self):
        self.assertEqual(Calculator().multiply(2.5, 2), 5.0)


if __name__ == '__main__':
    unittest.main()
```

### Exercise 5:  Writing Test Suites
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**:
1.  Using the previous `Calculator` class and `TestCalculator` class, create a separate `TestAdd` class using the `add` function from earlier exercises.
2.  Create a test suite that runs both `TestCalculator` and `TestAdd` test cases.

**Solution Rubric**:
-  Correct `TestAdd` class setup (3 points)
-  Correct test suite creation (5 points)
-  All tests run successfully (2 point)

```python
import unittest

class Calculator:
    def multiply(self, x, y):
        return x * y

def add(x, y):
    if not isinstance(x, (int, float)) or not isinstance(y, (int, float)):
        raise TypeError("Inputs must be numbers")
    return x + y

class TestCalculator(unittest.TestCase):
    def test_multiply_positive(self):
        self.assertEqual(Calculator().multiply(2, 3), 6)

    def test_multiply_negative(self):
        self.assertEqual(Calculator().multiply(-2, 3), -6)

    def test_multiply_float(self):
        self.assertEqual(Calculator().multiply(2.5, 2), 5.0)

class TestAdd(unittest.TestCase):
    def test_add_positive(self):
        self.assertEqual(add(2, 3), 5)

    def test_add_negative(self):
        self.assertEqual(add(-1, -2), -3)

    def test_add_float(self):
        self.assertEqual(add(1.5, 2.5), 4.0)

    def test_add_invalid_input(self):
        with self.assertRaises(TypeError):
            add("a", 2)

    def test_add_zero(self):
        self.assertEqual(add(0, 5), 5)


if __name__ == '__main__':
    suite = unittest.TestSuite()
    suite.addTest(unittest.makeSuite(TestCalculator))
    suite.addTest(unittest.makeSuite(TestAdd))

    runner = unittest.TextTestRunner()
    runner.run(suite)
```

# Writing Effective Unit Tests - Practice Materials

## Practice Exercises

### Exercise 1: Identifying Test Cases
**Type**: Multiple Choice
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 5 minutes

**Instructions**:
Which of the following is NOT a good characteristic of a well-designed unit test?

A) It tests a single, specific functionality.
B) It is independent of other tests.
C) It relies on external dependencies whenever possible.
D) It is repeatable and consistent.

**Answer**: C

### Exercise 2: Writing a Simple Test
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Beginner
**Estimated Time**: 15 minutes

**Instructions**:
Write a unit test using the `unittest` module to test the following function:

```python
def add(x, y):
  """Adds two numbers together."""
  return x + y
```

Ensure your test case covers the scenario where both `x` and `y` are positive integers.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria          | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                              |
|-------------------|--------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Correctness       | 5      | Test correctly asserts that the `add` function returns the correct sum for positive integers.                                                                           |
| Test Structure    | 3      | Test is properly structured within a `unittest.TestCase` class.                                                                                                         |
| Import Statement  | 2      | Correctly imports the `unittest` module.                                                                                                                                  |

**Expected Answer/Code**:

```python
import unittest

def add(x, y):
  """Adds two numbers together."""
  return x + y

class TestAdd(unittest.TestCase):
  def test_add_positive_numbers(self):
    self.assertEqual(add(2, 3), 5)

if __name__ == '__main__':
  unittest.main()
```

### Exercise 3: Handling Edge Cases
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 20 minutes

**Instructions**:
Extend the `TestAdd` class from Exercise 2 to include test cases that handle:

1.  Adding a positive number and zero.
2.  Adding two negative numbers.
3.  Adding a positive and a negative number.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria          | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                              |
|-------------------|--------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Correctness       | 9      | Tests correctly assert that the `add` function returns the correct sum for all specified scenarios. (3 points per scenario)                                                                           |
| Test Structure    | 3      | Tests are properly structured within the `unittest.TestCase` class.                                                                                                         |
| Clarity           | 3      | Tests are named descriptively and easy to understand.                                                                                                                                  |

**Expected Answer/Code**:

```python
import unittest

def add(x, y):
  """Adds two numbers together."""
  return x + y

class TestAdd(unittest.TestCase):
  def test_add_positive_numbers(self):
    self.assertEqual(add(2, 3), 5)

  def test_add_positive_and_zero(self):
    self.assertEqual(add(5, 0), 5)

  def test_add_negative_numbers(self):
    self.assertEqual(add(-2, -3), -5)

  def test_add_positive_and_negative(self):
    self.assertEqual(add(5, -2), 3)

if __name__ == '__main__':
  unittest.main()
```

### Exercise 4: Using `assertRaises`
**Type**: Coding
**Difficulty**: Intermediate
**Estimated Time**: 15 minutes

**Instructions**:
Write a function called `divide(x, y)` that divides `x` by `y`.  Raise a `ValueError` if `y` is zero. Then, write a unit test using `assertRaises` to ensure that the function correctly raises a `ValueError` when dividing by zero.

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria          | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                              |
|-------------------|--------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Function Correctness | 5      | The `divide` function correctly performs division and raises a `ValueError` when dividing by zero.                                                                      |
| Test Correctness   | 5      | The unit test correctly uses `assertRaises` to verify the `ValueError`.                                                                                                |
| Code Clarity       | 5      | The code is well-structured and easy to understand.                                                                                                                       |

**Expected Answer/Code**:

```python
import unittest

def divide(x, y):
  """Divides x by y. Raises ValueError if y is zero."""
  if y == 0:
    raise ValueError("Cannot divide by zero.")
  return x / y

class TestDivide(unittest.TestCase):
  def test_divide_by_zero(self):
    with self.assertRaises(ValueError):
      divide(10, 0)

if __name__ == '__main__':
  unittest.main()
```

### Exercise 6: Testing a Class Method
**Type**: Coding

**Estimated Time**: 10 minutes

**Instructions**:

Create a class called `Rectangle` with methods to calculate area and perimeter. Create a unit test to verify the `calculate_area` method.

```python
class Rectangle:
  def __init__(self, length, width):
    self.length = length
    self.width = width

  def calculate_area(self):
    return self.length * self.width
```

**Solution Rubric**:

| Criteria          | Points | Description                                                                                                                                                              |
|-------------------|--------|--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Class Definition  | 3      | `Rectangle` class is defined correctly.                                                                                                                               |
| Test Correctness   | 5      | Test accurately verifies the `calculate_area` method.                                                                                                                 |
| Code Structure     | 2      | Code is well-structured and readable.                                                                                                                                |

**Expected Answer/Code**:

```python
import unittest

class Rectangle:
  def __init__(self, length, width):
    self.length = length
    self.width = width

  def calculate_area(self):
    return self.length * self.width

class TestRectangle(unittest.TestCase):
  def test_calculate_area(self):
    rect = Rectangle(5, 10)
    self.assertEqual(rect.calculate_area(), 50)

if __name__ == '__main__':
  unittest.main()
```

Which Python module is commonly used for writing unit tests?

def factorial(n):

        return 1
    else:
        return n * factorial(n-1)

# Quality Assurance Report: Python Programming for B.Tech Students

This report assesses the quality of the "Python Programming for B.Tech Students" course materials. The evaluation focuses on curriculum alignment, completeness, accuracy, and clarity.

## 1. Course Overview

The course aims to provide B.Tech students with a comprehensive introduction to Python programming. The target audience is students with basic programming knowledge. The total duration is 60 hours, encompassing 27 lessons.

## 2. Scoring Summary

| Category             | Score |
| -------------------- | ----- |
| Curriculum Alignment | 85    |
| Completeness         | 70    |
| Accuracy             | 90    |
| Clarity              | 67    |
| **Overall Quality**  | **78**    |

The course **passes** the minimum quality threshold of 75%.

## 3. Detailed Assessment

### 3.1. Curriculum Alignment (85/100)

*   **Strengths:** The provided materials align well with the stated learning outcomes, particularly in introducing Python fundamentals and setting up the development environment. The learning objectives for Lesson 1 are clearly tied to the instruction content and practice exercises.
*   **Weaknesses:** The provided excerpt is missing the complete list of learning outcomes. Without the complete list, it is difficult to fully assess alignment of all course elements.

### 3.2. Completeness (70/100)

*   **Strengths:** The lesson preview includes an overview, learning objectives, instruction content, and practice materials, covering essential components of a well-structured lesson.
*   **Weaknesses:**
    *   The provided materials are incomplete. We only have a preview of Lesson 1 and snippets of the course overview and practice materials.
    *   The course description mentions "coding exercises, projects, and real-world examples," but the extent of these elements is not evident in the provided materials.
    *   Assessment methods beyond practice exercises are not described.
    *   The full list of course lessons is not provided.

### 3.3. Accuracy (90/100)

*   **Strengths:** The provided content appears to be technically accurate and up-to-date. The description of Python's features and its uses in various domains is consistent with current industry practices.
*   **Weaknesses:** No significant inaccuracies were found in the provided material.

### 3.4. Clarity (67/100)

*   **Strengths:** The language used is generally accessible to B.Tech students with some programming experience.
*   **Weaknesses:**
    *   The level of detail in the "Instruction Content" section of Lesson 1 is somewhat superficial. More in-depth explanations and examples would enhance understanding.
    *   The connection between the theory and practice exercises could be strengthened. For example, after explaining data types, the exercise could involve writing code to manipulate different data types.
    *   Some sections may benefit from visual aids (diagrams, flowcharts) to illustrate complex concepts.

## 4. Issues and Recommendations

| Issue                                        | Severity | Recommendation                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| -------------------------------------------- | -------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Incomplete course materials                   | **Critical** | Provide the complete curriculum, including all lesson plans, practice materials, and assessment details.                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| Limited depth in instruction content          | **Major**  | Expand the "Instruction Content" sections to provide more in-depth explanations, examples, and demonstrations of key concepts.                                                                                                                                                      |
| Weak connection between theory and practice   | **Major**  | Design practice exercises that directly apply the concepts taught in the instruction content. Include coding exercises that require students to use the learned concepts to solve problems.                                                                                              |
| Lack of visual aids                           | **Minor**  | Incorporate visual aids such as diagrams, flowcharts, and code snippets to enhance understanding and engagement.                                                                                                                                                                |
| Unclear assessment methods beyond exercises | **Minor**  | Detail all assessment methods used in the course, including projects, quizzes, and exams. Explain how these assessments align with the learning outcomes.                                                                                                                              |
| Missing full list of learning outcomes     | **Critical** |  Provide the complete learning outcomes of the course. Each learning outcome should be SMART (Specific, Measurable, Achievable, Relevant, Time-bound).                                                                                                                                |

## 5. Conclusion

The "Python Programming for B.Tech Students" course shows promise, but requires improvements to ensure completeness, clarity, and a stronger connection between theory and practice. Addressing the identified issues will significantly enhance the overall quality and effectiveness of the course.
